<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Ainokaze Toyama Railway</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p>The <b>Ainokaze Toyama Railway</b> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">あいの風とやま鉄道株式会社</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Ainokaze Toyama Tetsudō Kabushiki-gaisha</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> is a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership#Japan" title="Public–private partnership">third-sector</a> railway operating company established in 2012 to operate passenger railway services on the section of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JR_West" title="JR West">JR West</a> <a href="/wiki/Hokuriku_Main_Line" title="Hokuriku Main Line">Hokuriku Main Line</a> within <a href="/wiki/Toyama_Prefecture" title="Toyama Prefecture">Toyama Prefecture</a> when it was separated from the JR West network in March 2015, coinciding with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Hokuriku_Shinkansen" title="Hokuriku Shinkansen">Hokuriku Shinkansen</a> extension from <a href="/wiki/Nagano_Station" title="Nagano Station">Nagano</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kanazawa_Station" title="Kanazawa Station">Kanazawa</a>. The company was founded on 24 July 2012, and has its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Toyama,_Toyama" title="Toyama, Toyama">Toyama, Toyama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-overview-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shareholders">Shareholders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Shareholders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Toyama_Prefecture" title="Toyama Prefecture">Toyama Prefecture</a> is the main shareholder, owning 63% of the company's shares, 27% is owned by municipalities within Toyama Prefecture, and 10% is owned by private-sector businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-overview-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<p>From 14 March 2015, the Ainokaze Toyama Railway took over control of local passenger operations on the 100.1 km section JR West <a href="/wiki/Hokuriku_Main_Line" title="Hokuriku Main Line">Hokuriku Main Line</a> between <a href="/wiki/Ichiburi_Station" title="Ichiburi Station">Ichiburi</a> in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Niigata_Prefecture" title="Niigata Prefecture">Niigata Prefecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurikara_Station" title="Kurikara Station">Kurikara</a> in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Ishikawa_Prefecture" title="Ishikawa Prefecture">Ishikawa Prefecture</a>, with a total of 21 stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Service_outline">Service outline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Service outline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While the Ainokaze Toyama Railway Line officially stretches from Kurikara in the west to Ichiburi in the east, most services terminate at <a href="/wiki/Tomari_Station_(Toyama)" title="Tomari Station (Toyama)">Tomari</a> to the east, with a same-platform transfer provided to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Echigo_Tokimeki_Railway_Nihonkai_Hisui_Line" title="Echigo Tokimeki Railway Nihonkai Hisui Line">Echigo Tokimeki Railway Nihonkai Hisui Line</a> services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup> Some through services continue over the Echigo Tokimeki Railway Nihonkai Hisui Line to and from <a href="/wiki/Itoigawa_Station" title="Itoigawa Station">Itoigawa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup> To the west, most services continue to and from <a href="/wiki/Kanazawa_Station" title="Kanazawa Station">Kanazawa</a> over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IR_Ishikawa_Railway_Line" title="IR Ishikawa Railway Line">IR Ishikawa Railway Line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup> In addition to all-stations "Local" <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">普通</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>futsū</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> services, limited-stop "Rapid" services named <i>Ainokaze Liner</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">あいの風ライナー</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> operate between Tomari and Toyama or Kanazawa during the weekday morning and evening peaks. A supplementary liner fare of 300 yen is required to board these services, and all seats are reserved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/ICOCA" title="ICOCA">ICOCA</a> and other compatible IC farecards can be used on the line since 26 March 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Services on the line use a fleet of 16 two-car <a href="/wiki/521_series" title="521 series">521 series</a> (2nd-batch type) <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric multiple unit</a> (EMU) trains and five three-car <a href="/wiki/413_series" title="413 series">413 series</a> EMUs (former sets B01 to B03, B07, and B10) acquired from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JR_West" title="JR West">JR West</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-railfan650_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-railfan650-3">[3]</a></sup> The 521 series trains will receive a new livery with a blue wave design on the seaward (north) side and a green wave design on the landward (south) side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup> While both the Ainokaze Toyama Railway and neighbouring IR Ishikawa Railway operate similar 521 series trains, the respective operators' trains do not run coupled together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dj371_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-dj371-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 1 April 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the 521 series and 413 series fleets are as follows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jrr2015_summer_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-jrr2015_summer-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_developments">Future developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Future developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An additional 521 series set is to be ordered during fiscal 2016 or 2017, and one of the 413 series sets is to be modified for use as a special-event train in the first half of fiscal 2016, with new seat covers and a new external livery. The train will also be used to provide additional capacity on regular services during the peak periods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ainokaze20151116_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-ainokaze20151116-5">[5]</a></sup> From the first half of fiscal 2018, a 413 series set will be rebuilt as a tourist train, returning to service on the line in the second half of fiscal 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ainokaze20151116_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-ainokaze20151116-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The company was founded on 24 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-overview-1">[1]</a></sup> The company name "Ainokaze Toyama Railway" was announced on 30 May 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mynavi20130531_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-mynavi20130531-6">[6]</a></sup> <i>Ainokaze</i> refers to a north-easterly breeze that blows in the region in spring and summer, and is mentioned in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manyoshu" title="Manyoshu">Manyoshu</a></i> collection of Japanese poetry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mynavi20130531_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-mynavi20130531-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The company was formally granted a railway operating license by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Land,_Infrastructure,_Transport_and_Tourism" title="Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism">Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism</a> on 28 February 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mlit20140226_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-mlit20140226-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_developments_2">Future developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ainokaze_Toyama_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Future developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>New stations are planned to be built between Takaoka and Nishi-Takaoka, and between Toyama and Higashi-Toyama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mynavi20130531_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-mynavi20130531-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Toyama_City_Tram_Line" title="Toyama City Tram Line">Toyama City Tram Line</a> (<i>Shiden</i>)
